Nafaqah — Maintenance
intermediate
6 min
Obligation of Wealthy Relatives to Spend When Husband is Poor
Stating the ruling that a wealthy relative must provide maintenance and can recover from the husband.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a wealthy relative must provide maintenance to a poor woman when her husband is poor and can recover the amount from the husband later.

Core Idea
Wealthy relative must support the woman and can recover from the husband when he becomes able.

When a husband is too poor to provide maintenance, the burden does not simply fall on the wife. Sharh al-Mukhtar outlines a clear obligation on wealthy relatives—like a son from another husband or a brother—to step in. This obligation is not a voluntary loan but a commanded duty based on ma'ruf, with a legal mechanism for recovery from the husband when his financial situation improves.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core scenario
Pinpoint the three parties: a poor woman, her poor husband, and a wealthy relative (son from another husband or brother).
The relative must be one who would owe maintenance if the husband were absent.
2
State the ruling and its basis
The relative is obligated to spend on the woman's maintenance. This is wajib because it is part of ma'ruf (good conduct).
Ma'ruf is a recognized legal basis in Hanafi fiqh for obligations beyond the nuclear family.
3
Explain the recovery mechanism
The relative can claim the amount spent from the husband when the husband becomes wealthy (yusr). The relative can be imprisoned if he refuses to spend.
This is a claim for reimbursement, not a gift.
4
Apply to young children
The same principle applies to the maintenance of young children of a poor father: grandmother, brother, uncle must spend and recover from the father later.
Adult children are excluded—their maintenance is treated differently.
5
Distinguish from borrowing
The passage clarifies that this is not simply borrowing (istidana) but a direct command to the relative. The relative's obligation is primary in this situation.
Other relatives or strangers may be involved through borrowing, but the wealthy relative is directly obligated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأطلق في الاستدانة فشمل قريب المرأة والأجنبي ولكن ذكر في شرح المختار أن المرأة المعسرة إذا كان زوجها معسراً ولها ابن من غيره موسر أو أخ موسر فنفقتها على زوجها ويؤمر الابن أو الأخ بالإنفاق عليها ويرجع به على الزوج إذا أيسر ويحبس الابن أو الأخ إذا امتنع لأن هذا من المعروف قال الزيعلي : فتبين بهذا أن الإدانة لنفقتها إذا كان الزوج معسراً وهي معسرة تجب على من كانت تجب عليه نفقتها لولا الزوج، وعلى هذا لو كان للمعسر أولاد صغار ولم يقدر على إنفاقهم تجب نفقتهم على من تجب عليه لولا الأب كالأم والأخ والعم ثم ترجع به على الأب إذا أيسر بخلاف نفقة أولاده الكبار
And borrowing was made general, so it includes a relative of the woman and a stranger. But it was mentioned in Sharh al-Mukhtar that a poor woman whose husband is poor and she has a son from another husband who is wealthy or a wealthy brother, her maintenance is on her husband, and the son or brother is ordered to spend on her and will recover it from the husband when he becomes wealthy, and the son or brother is imprisoned if he refuses, because this is a matter of ma'ruf (good conduct). Al-Zayla'i said: It becomes clear from this that borrowing for her maintenance when the husband is poor and she is poor is obligatory on the one who would have been obligated to spend on her if not for the husband. Based on this, if a poor man has young children and cannot support them, their maintenance is obligatory on the one who would be obligated if not for the father, such as the mother, brother, and paternal uncle; then they recover it from the father when he becomes wealthy, unlike the maintenance of his adult children.
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This passage extends the previous discussion on borrowing. The author notes that the ruling on borrowing is general, including both relatives and strangers. However, in Sharh al-Mukhtar, there is a specific ruling: if the husband is poor and the woman has a wealthy son from a previous marriage or a wealthy brother, they are ordered to spend on her. This is not simply borrowing; it is an obligation based on ma'ruf. They can then recover the amount from the husband when he becomes wealthy. If they refuse, they can be imprisoned. Al-Zayla'i explains that this obligation is on those who would have been obliged to support her if not for the husband. This principle also applies to the maintenance of young children of a poor father: their maintenance falls on relatives like the mother, brother, or uncle, who can then recover from the father when he becomes wealthy. This is specific to young children; for adult children, it is different.

Key Terms
معروف (ma'rūf): A legally recognized good deed; here it refers to the obligation of relatives to support each other in need.
إعسار (i'sār): Poverty or inability to pay maintenance.
يسر (yusr): Wealth or ability to pay.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When the husband is poor, who is ordered to spend on the wife?
A) Her father
B) Her wealthy son from another husband or brother
C) Any stranger
D) The judge

Key Takeaway
The duty to support a relative in need can require a wealthy son or brother to provide maintenance and then recover the amount from the liable husband when he becomes able.

Nafaqah — Maintenance

8 min
Dispute on Judicial Annulment Due to Husband's Inability to Provide Maintenance
A fatwa-level dispute analysis from al-Bahr al-Rā’iq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on faskh for inability to maintain, identify the key condition (presence vs absence) that divides them, and evaluate the practical consequence of the khilaf.

Core Idea
Hanafi maslaha: no faskh for inability when the husband is absent; only presence triggers judicial intervention.

This lesson examines a well-known inter-madhhab dispute: can a wife obtain a judicial annulment (faskh) because her husband cannot provide maintenance, if the husband is physically absent? The Hanafi and Shafi'i schools answer differently based on their understanding of the effective cause (‘illah) and the scope of ijtihad. The passage from al-Bahr al-Rā’iq clarifies the Hanafi stance: faskh for ‘ajz is only open to ijtihad when the husband is present. Let us walk through the arguments and the practical impact.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
According to the Hanafi school, faskh due to the husband's inability to pay maintenance is permissible only when the husband is present in the locality. If he is absent, the wife cannot seek faskh on grounds of ‘ajz; she must wait or seek other remedies.
The basis is that the ‘illah (effective cause) is the immediate harm of non-maintenance combined with the possibility of coercion, which only exists when he is present.
2
Identify the opposing school
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that faskh is permissible regardless of the husband's presence or absence, provided his inability is proven. For the Shafi'is, the ‘illah is the inability itself, not the possibility of direct enforcement.
This broader view leads to a more accessible remedy for the wife.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi mashāyikh (later authorities) assert that the case of absence is not open to independent reasoning (ijtihād) within the school. Thus, a qāḍī cannot rule based on absence; any such ruling would be invalid and unenforceable.
This effectively limits faskh in the Hanafi court to cases where the husband is present and unable.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
In practice, a Hanafi judge in a Hanafi jurisdiction will not annul a marriage for inability if the husband is absent. A Shafi'i judge will. This difference affects women's access to dissolution based on poverty.
The khilaf is real and impacts forum shopping in mixed-madhhab contexts.
5
Evaluate the muftā bihī
The relied-upon position for fatwā in the Hanafi school is that no faskh occurs in absence. This is the position of the classical texts and the consensus of later authorities.
This tarjīh is based on the principle that absence removes the possibility of immediate enforcement and coercion, which the Hanafis consider a necessary condition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الدرر صرحت اختلاف في الفسخ حينئذ . وعلى هذا فلا فرق في الفسخ بالعجز بين حضوره وغيبته خلافاً لما فهمه من أن الفسخ حال غيبته غير منوط بالعجز بل بترك الإنفاق مع القدرة وليس كذلك اهـ . ما في حاشية أبي السعود والحاصل أن التفريق حال حضرته وحال غيبته جائز عند الشافعي إذا ثبت عجزه، والأول اعتبره مشايخنا مجتهداً فيه دون الثاني ويصح القضاء بالأول وتنفيذه دون الثاني
The pearls clarified that there is a difference of opinion on faskh then. And based on this, there is no difference in faskh due to inability between his presence and his absence, contrary to what was understood that faskh during his absence is not contingent on inability but rather on withholding maintenance despite ability, and it is not so. End of what is in Hashiyat Abi al-Su'ud. The summary: Separation in his presence and in his absence is permissible according to al-Shafi'i if his inability is proven. Our mashayikh considered the first (presence) as an ijtihad matter, not the second. And the ruling can be made according to the first and enforced, but not according to the second.
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This passage discusses the Hanafi position on judicial annulment (faskh) due to the husband's inability to provide maintenance. The author cites from Hashiyat Abi al-Su'ud that some understood that faskh during absence is based on failure to spend despite ability, but the correct view is that it is based on inability. The summary states that Imam al-Shafi'i permits faskh in both presence and absence if inability is proven. The Hanafi mashayikh only allow ijtihad (independent reasoning) in the case of presence; the case of absence is not open to ijtihad. Therefore, a judge's ruling based on the first (presence) is valid and enforceable, but not based on the second (absence).

Key Terms
فسخ (faskh): Judicial dissolution of marriage due to a defect or failure to fulfill obligations.
عجز ('ajz): Inability to pay maintenance.
حضور (ḥuḍūr): The husband's presence in the locality where the wife resides.
غيبة (ghayba): The husband's absence from the locality.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is judicial annulment (faskh) for inability to provide maintenance valid?
A) In both the husband's presence and absence
B) Only if the husband is absent
C) Only if the husband is present
D) Never

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school conditions faskh for inability on the husband's presence; absence renders the annulment invalid.

Nafaqah — Maintenance

The Rule of Past Maintenance and Enforcement
Ruling on past maintenance and enforcement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for past maintenance to become owed and identify the enforcement measures against a wealthy husband who refuses to pay.

Core Idea
Past maintenance is not automatically recovered; a judge's decree or husband's consent is required.

In Hanafi law, a husband's obligation to provide maintenance is ongoing, but what about periods when he was poor and could not pay? This passage clarifies that past maintenance does not become due later unless a judge decreed it or the husband agreed. It also outlines the practical enforcement when a wealthy husband refuses, emphasizing coercive measures like selling property or imprisonment rather than dissolving the marriage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling on past maintenance
Read the opening sentence: 'And maintenance for the past is not obligatory except by a judge's decree or by consent.' Note that the obligation does not arise retroactively; it requires a formal decree or voluntary agreement.
The rule applies even if the husband later becomes wealthy.
2
Understand the rationale and the exception
The text explains that past maintenance is like a dead person – obligation does not exist during poverty. However, there is an exception: if the wife cannot find a stranger to lend or sell on credit, then her son or close relatives are obliged to help. If she can find such a person, she should rely on them first.
3
Examine the enforcement procedure against a wealthy refuser
If the husband is wealthy but refuses to spend, the judge does not annul the marriage. Instead, he sells the husband's property to cover maintenance. If no property is found, the husband is imprisoned until he pays.
This approach maintains the marriage bond while enforcing the obligation.
4
Analyze the limits on what can be sold
Scholars discuss what assets can be sold. Basic necessities like dwelling and servant are exempt. Clothes: some say leave one set, others two sets. Fine clothes can be sold to buy moderate ones and the remainder used for debts.
This balances the wife's right with the husband's basic dignity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا تجب نفقة مضت إلا بالقضاء أو الرضا . حيث لا يرجع عليه بعد اليسار لأنها لا تجب مع الإعسار فكان كالميت اهـ. وأقره عليه في فتح القدير. وينبغي أن يكون محله إذا لم تجد أجنبياً يبيعها بالنسيئة أو يقرضها فحينئذ يتعين على ولدها ونحوه، وأما إذا وجدت فلا وفي فتح القدير ولو امتنع من الإنفاق عليها مع اليسر لم يفرق ويبيع الحاكم ما له عليه وصرفه في نفقتها، فإن لم يجد ما له يحبسه حتى ينفق عليها ولا يفسخ .اهـ. وفي المجتبى والذخيرة : قال الزوج في مجلس أبي يوسف ليس عندي نفقة فقال خذي عمامته وأنفقيها على نفسك، فيحتمل أنه علم أبو يوسف أن له عمامة أخرى وإلا لاتباع العمامة في النفقة وسائر الديون. قال الخصاف : ولا يبيع ما مسكنه وخادمه ويبيع ذلك ، وقيل ما سوى الإزار، وقيل يترك لنفسه دستاً يبيع من الثياب ويبيع ذلك، وقيل دستين وبه قال السرخسي ولو كان له ثياب حسنة يمكنه الاكتفاء بما دونها يبيعها ويشتري ذلك ببعضها ويصرف الباقي إلى الديون والنفقة .اهـ. وسيأتي تمامه في الحبس وفي باب الحجر
And maintenance for the past is not obligatory except by a judge's decree or by consent. So he does not recover it from him after he becomes wealthy, because it is not obligatory during poverty, so it is like a dead person. End. And he affirmed it in Fath al-Qadir. And it should be that its place is when she does not find a stranger who will sell to her on credit or lend to her; then her son and the like are specifically obliged. But if she finds such a person, then no. And in Fath al-Qadir: If he refuses to spend on her while he is wealthy, he is not separated; rather, the judge sells whatever he has against him and spends it on her maintenance. If he does not find any property, he imprisons him until he spends on her, and he does not annul the marriage. End. And in al-Mujtaba and al-Dhakhira: The husband said in the court of Abu Yusuf, 'I have no maintenance,' so he said, 'Take his turban and spend it on yourself.' It is possible that Abu Yusuf knew he had another turban; otherwise, the turban would not be taken for maintenance and other debts. Al-Khassaf said: Do not sell his dwelling and his servant; sell other than that. Some said: except the lower garment. Some said: leave for himself a set of clothing to sell? [Actually, the text says: 'يترك لنفسه دستاً يبيع من الثياب ويبيع ذلك' meaning leave for himself a set and sell that?] Some said two sets, and al-Sarakhsi said that. If he has fine clothing and can manage with less, he sells them, buys modest ones with part of the proceeds, and spends the remainder on debts and maintenance. End. The rest will follow in the chapter on imprisonment and the chapter on interdiction.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage covers two important rules. First, maintenance for past days when the husband was poor is not owed after he becomes wealthy, unless a judge decreed it or the husband agreed. This is because the obligation does not exist during poverty, similar to a dead person. The author from Fath al-Qadir adds that this applies when the wife cannot find a stranger to lend or sell on credit; otherwise, she should take from that person, and her relatives are not obligated. Second, when the husband is wealthy but refuses to spend, the judge does not annul the marriage. Instead, he sells the husband's property for maintenance. If no property is found, the husband is imprisoned until he pays. Abu Yusuf famously told a woman to take her husband's turban. Scholars then discuss what can be sold: basic necessities like dwelling and servant are exempt. Most say to sell clothes beyond one or two sets. This shows the Hanafi preference for enforcing payment rather than dissolving the marriage.

Key Terms
نفقة ماضية (nafaqa māḍiya): Maintenance for a period already passed, which is not automatically owed.
قضاء (qaḍā'): A judge's decree establishing a financial obligation.
رضا (riḍā): The husband's consent to pay past maintenance.
حبس (ḥabs): Imprisonment as a coercive measure to enforce payment of maintenance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi text, what is the first step a judge should take when a wealthy husband refuses to pay maintenance?
A) Imprison the husband immediately.
B) Annul the marriage.
C) Sell the husband's property (excluding essentials) to cover maintenance.
D) Order the wife to find a creditor.

Key Takeaway
Past maintenance requires a judge's decree or husband's consent; enforcement against a wealthy refuser uses property sale and imprisonment, not annulment.

Nafaqah — Maintenance
intermediate
8 min
Completing Maintenance When Husband Becomes Wealthy: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Analyzing the ruling on claiming full wealthy maintenance after status change and the dispute between Karkhi and Khassaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on claiming increased maintenance after a change in financial status and evaluate the intra-madhhab disagreement between al-Karkhi and al-Khassaf.

Core Idea
A wife can always demand increased maintenance when the husband's wealth improves, even if the judge had decreed a lower amount.

In Hanafi maintenance law, the amount of nafaqah varies with the financial status of the husband. But what happens when a judge has already decreed maintenance based on poverty, and the husband later becomes wealthy? This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq examines the rule and addresses a dispute between two early Hanafi authorities, al-Karkhi and al-Khassaf, regarding whose status is considered. Al-Zayla'i thought the ruling only worked on al-Karkhi's view, but the author refutes this, showing it holds on both views.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
The passage states that if a judge decreed poor maintenance, and then the husband becomes wealthy, the wife can demand completion of the wealthy maintenance. This is because maintenance differs with financial status and the decree was for a past period.
The ruling is about a change in circumstances after the decree.
2
Understand the Karkhi vs. Khassaf dispute
Al-Karkhi holds that only the husband's status determines maintenance. Al-Khassaf holds that both the husband's and wife's statuses matter. Al-Zayla'i claimed the matn's ruling only works on al-Karkhi's view.
The apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah) follows al-Karkhi, but the relied-upon view is al-Khassaf's.
3
Analyze al-Zayla'i's criticism
Al-Zayla'i argued that the author of the matn contradicted himself by starting with al-Khassaf's view and then giving a ruling that only fits al-Karkhi's view, creating a tension.
This criticism is recorded in the commentary.
4
Follow the author's rebuttal
The author responds that the matn's statement is general and covers all scenarios. If both spouses become wealthy, it's agreed. If only the husband becomes wealthy, al-Khassaf's view yields the middle level (al-wasaṭ), which is an increase from poor maintenance, so the ruling holds. Similarly, if only the wife becomes wealthy, the maintenance is the middle level from her side. Thus, no contradiction exists.
The author demonstrates that the ruling is sound on all views.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وتمم نفقة اليسار بطروّه وأن قضى بنفقة الأعسار) لأن النفقة تختلف اليسار والإعسار وما قضى به تقدير لنفقة لم تجب فإذا تبدل حاله فلها المطالبة بتمام حقها . وزعم الشارح الزيعلي أن هذه المسألة تستقيم على قول الكرخي حيث اعتبر حال الرجل فقط ولم يعتبر حال المرأة أصلاً وهو ظاهر الرواية، ولا يستقيم على ما ذكره الخصاف من اعتبار حالهما على ما عليه الاعتماد فيكون فيه نوع تناقض من الشيخ لأن ما ذكره أول الباب هو قول الخصاف ثم ثنى الحكم على قول الكرخي .اهـ وأقره عليه في فتح القدير وهو مردود بل هو مستقيم على قول الكل لأن الخلاف إنما يظهر فيما إذا كان أحدهما موسراً والآخر معسراً، وكلام المصنف هنا أعم من ذلك، فلو كانا معسرين وقضى بنفقة الإعسار ثم أيسرا نفقة اليسار اتفاقاً، وإذا أيسر الرجل وحده فإنه يقضي بنفقة يساره ونفقة يساره في حال إعسارها عند الخصاف هي الوسط، وكذا إذا أيسرت المرأة وحدها قضى بنفقة يسارها وهي الوسط عنده فصر كلامه شاملاً للصور الثلاث بهذا الاعتبار لأنه لم يقيد بيسار الزوج . فإنه يتمم بمنزلة الميت ا هـ فتأمل وسيأتي هناك جوابه
His statement: (And he completes the maintenance of wealth when it arrives, even if he decreed maintenance of poverty) because maintenance differs between wealth and poverty, and what is decreed is an estimate for a maintenance that was not due; so if his condition changes, she has the right to demand her full right. Al-Zayla'i the commentator claimed that this issue is only sound according to al-Karkhi's view, who considered only the man's condition and not the woman's at all, and that is the apparent narration. But it is not sound according to what al-Khassaf mentioned, which is relying on considering both their conditions; so there is a kind of contradiction from the shaykh, because what he mentioned at the beginning of the chapter is al-Khassaf's view, then he gave a ruling based on al-Karkhi's view. End. And he affirmed it in Fath al-Qadir, but it is refuted; rather, it is sound according to all, because the difference only appears when one is wealthy and the other poor. The author's statement here is more general than that. So if both are poor and he decreed poor maintenance, then they both become wealthy, the wealthy maintenance is by agreement. If only the man becomes wealthy, then he decrees wealthy maintenance; and the wealthy maintenance when she is poor according to al-Khassaf is the middle. Similarly, if only the woman becomes wealthy, he decrees her wealthy maintenance, which is the middle according to him. So his statement encompasses all three scenarios in this consideration, because he did not restrict it to the man's wealth. So he completes it, like a dead person. End. So ponder. And the answer will come there.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage addresses the rule that if a judge decreed maintenance based on the husband's poverty, and then the husband becomes wealthy, the wife can demand the full maintenance due a wealthy woman. The author explains that this ruling is agreed upon when both spouses become wealthy. The dispute is when only one becomes wealthy. Al-Zayla'i claimed the ruling only works on al-Karkhi's view, which considers only the man's status. But the author refutes this, saying the statement of the matn is more general and works on both views. Even according to al-Khassaf, who considers both, when the man becomes wealthy alone, the maintenance is the middle level; when the woman becomes wealthy alone, it is also the middle. Thus, the ruling is consistent across the board. This shows that the wife can always claim an increase in maintenance when the husband's financial status improves, regardless of her own status.

Key Terms
نفقة اليسار (nafaqa al-yasār): Maintenance appropriate for a wealthy person.
نفقة الإعسار (nafaqa al-i'sār): Maintenance appropriate for a poor person.
الوسط (al-wasaṭ): The middle level of maintenance, between that of a wealthy and a poor person.
الكرخي (al-Karkhī): Abū al-Ḥasan al-Karkhī, a prominent early Hanafi jurist who held that maintenance is determined solely by the husband's financial status.
الخصاف (al-Khaṣṣāf): Ahmad ibn 'Umar al-Khassaf, a Hanafi jurist who held that maintenance is determined by the conditions of both spouses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Khassaf, what level of maintenance is due when the husband becomes wealthy but the wife remains poor?
A) The full wealthy maintenance
B) The middle level (al-wasaṭ)
C) The poor maintenance
D) No maintenance

Key Takeaway
A wife can always demand an increase in maintenance when her husband's financial status improves, even if the judge had previously decreed a lower amount; the exact amount may vary depending on whether both spouses' statuses are considered.

Nafaqah — Maintenance
intermediate
6 min
Adjustment of Maintenance When Financial Status Changes: Harmonizing al-Karkhi and al-Khassaf
Commentary harmonizing two Hanafi views on maintenance adjustment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on adjusting maintenance when financial status changes, distinguishing between the views of al-Karkhi and al-Khassaf, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Maintenance adjusts upon change; the relied-upon view considers both spouses' conditions, yielding a middle level when only one is wealthy.

This lesson resolves an apparent contradiction within the Hanafi school. The author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq ruled that maintenance must be increased from the hardship level to the ease level when the husband becomes wealthy. Commentators noted a potential tension between two Hanafi authorities: al-Karkhi (considering only the husband) and al-Khassaf (considering both spouses). By examining the three possible scenarios of financial change, we see that the ruling is consistent with both views, and the relied-upon (mufta bihi) is the middle level when only one spouse is wealthy.

Guided Path
1
State the core ruling
Identify what the matn says: maintenance must be completed to the level of ease (nafaqat al-yasar) when ease occurs, even if the judge had previously set maintenance at the hardship level (nafaqat al-i'sar).
This establishes the principle of dynamic adjustment.
2
Identify the two Hanafi opinions
Understand that al-Karkhi considers only the husband's financial status, while al-Khassaf considers both spouses. The relied-upon view is al-Khassaf's.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
3
Analyze the three possible scenarios
Work through the scenarios: both become wealthy, only husband becomes wealthy, only wife becomes wealthy. In the first, maintenance of ease is agreed. In the latter two, al-Khassaf's view gives the middle level (al-wasat).
The author's wording covers all three because he did not restrict to husband's ease.
4
Apply al-Khassaf's view to determine the ruling
For the scenario where only the husband becomes wealthy: the maintenance is the middle level (al-wasat). For only the wife becomes wealthy: also the middle level.
This reconciles the apparent contradiction.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position for fatwa is al-Khassaf's view: the middle level when one spouse is poor and the other wealthy.
This is what a judge applies in practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وتمم نفقة اليسار بطروّه وأن قضى بنفقة الأعسار) لأن النفقة تختلف اليسار والإعسار وما قضى به تقدير لنفقة لم تجب فإذا تبدل حاله فلها المطالبة بتمام حقها . وزعم الشارح الزيعلي أن هذه المسألة تستقيم على قول الكرخي حيث اعتبر حال الرجل فقط ولم يعتبر حال المرأة أصلاً وهو ظاهر الرواية، ولا يستقيم على ما ذكره الخصاف من اعتبار حالهما على ما عليه الاعتماد فيكون فيه نوع تناقض من الشيخ لأن ما ذكره أول الباب هو قول الخصاف ثم ثنى الحكم على قول الكرخي .اهـ وأقره عليه في فتح القدير وهو مردود بل هو مستقيم على قول الكل لأن الخلاف إنما يظهر فيما إذا كان أحدهما موسراً والآخر معسراً، وكلام المصنف هنا أعم من ذلك، فلو كانا معسرين وقضى بنفقة الإعسار ثم أيسرا نفقة اليسار اتفاقاً، وإذا أيسر الرجل وحده فإنه يقضي بنفقة يساره ونفقة يساره في حال إعسارها عند الخصاف هي الوسط، وكذا إذا أيسرت المرأة وحدها قضى بنفقة يسارها وهي الوسط عنده فصر كلامه شاملاً للصور الثلاث بهذا الاعتبار لأنه لم يقيد بيسار الزوج .
His statement: (And complete maintenance of ease upon its occurrence, even if he judged for maintenance of hardship) because maintenance differs between ease and hardship, and what he judged is an estimation for maintenance that was not obligatory. So if his situation changes, she may demand her full right. The commentator al-Zayla'i claimed that this issue is consistent only with al-Karkhi's opinion, who considered only the husband's condition and not the wife's at all, and that is the apparent narration; but it is not consistent with what al-Khassaf mentioned of considering both their conditions, which is the relied-upon view. Thus there is a kind of contradiction from the author because what he mentioned at the beginning of the chapter is al-Khassaf's view, then he ruled according to al-Karkhi's view. So it ends. And he affirmed it in Fath al-Qadir. But it is refuted; rather it is consistent with everyone's view because the disagreement only appears when one is wealthy and the other is poor, and the author's words here are more general than that. If both were poor and he judged for maintenance of hardship, then they become wealthy, maintenance of ease is agreed upon. If the husband alone becomes wealthy, then he is judged for maintenance of his ease, and his ease maintenance while she is poor according to al-Khassaf is the middle. Likewise, if the wife alone becomes wealthy, she is judged for maintenance of her ease, which is the middle according to him. So his statement includes the three scenarios in this consideration because he did not restrict it to the husband's ease.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (expansion probe) clarifying a ruling from the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding adjustment of maintenance. The author explains that when a judge has previously set maintenance based on the husband's hardship (i'sar), and later the husband becomes wealthy (yasar), the wife can demand an increase to the maintenance of the wealthy. The commentator al-Zayla'i raised a potential contradiction: the author's earlier statement followed al-Khassaf's view (considering both spouses' financial status), but this ruling seems to follow al-Karkhi (considering only the husband). The rebuttal states that there is no contradiction: the author's wording covers three scenarios: both become wealthy, only the husband, or only the wife. In each case, the maintenance is adjusted accordingly. On al-Khassaf's view, when one spouse is poor and the other wealthy, the maintenance is the middle level (al-wasat). This harmonizes the positions.

Key Terms
نفقة اليسار (nafaqat al-yasar): Maintenance appropriate for a wealthy person (the husband's obligation when he is well-off).
نفقة الإعسار (nafaqat al-i'sar): Maintenance appropriate for a poor person (the husband's obligation when he is in hardship).
الوسط (al-wasat): Middle level of maintenance, applicable when one spouse is wealthy and the other poor according to al-Khassaf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon view (al-Khassaf), if the husband is wealthy but the wife is poor, what level of maintenance is due?
A) Full maintenance of the wealthy
B) Maintenance of the poor
C) The middle level (al-wasat)
D) No maintenance until she becomes wealthy

Key Takeaway
When financial status changes, maintenance adjusts; the Hanafi relied-upon view considers both spouses' conditions, leading to a middle level when only one is wealthy.

Past Maintenance Does Not Accumulate as Debt Without Judge's Order or Mutual Agreement
Commentary on the ruling that past maintenance does not become a debt without a judicial order or mutual agreement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that past maintenance does not become a debt unless fixed by a judge or agreed upon, and explain the legal reasoning distinguishing maintenance from mahr.

Core Idea
Maintenance is a gift, not a debt — it only becomes binding through qada' or rida.

This passage clarifies a critical distinction in Hanafi family law: past maintenance does not automatically turn into an enforceable debt. The author explains why by contrasting maintenance (silah) with mahr (iwad). Understanding this rule is essential to know when a wife can claim unpaid maintenance legally.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the rule: past maintenance is not obligatory as a debt except with qada' (judicial order) or rida (mutual agreement).
The ruling is explicit in the matn.
2
Understand the key distinction
Why is maintenance different? Because it is classified as silah (gift), not 'iwad (consideration). Contrast with mahr, which is 'iwad and becomes a debt immediately.
This distinction is the core of the proof.
3
Follow the analogy
Maintenance is analogized to a gift (hibah): in a gift, ownership is not complete without possession (qabd). Similarly, maintenance obligation is not firmly established without qada' or rida.
The analogy is a qiyas jali.
4
Note the exception
For very short periods (less than a month), the maintenance may not lapse even without qada' or rida, to avoid hardship.
This exception is mentioned in al-Ghayah and al-Dhakhirah.
5
Avoid the common error
'Rida' means a prior agreement on a fixed amount, not retroactive consent after the period has passed.
The author explicitly corrects this misunderstanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولا تجب نفقة مضت إلا بالقضاء أو الرضا لأن النفقة صلة وليست بعوض عندنا فلم يستحكم الوجوب فيها إلا بالقضاء كالهبة لا توجب الملك فيها إلا بمؤكد وهو القبض، والصلح بمنزلة القضاء لأن ولايته على نفسه أقوى من ولاية القاضي بخلاف المهر لأنه عوض البضع والمراد بعدم وجوبها عدم كونها ديناً عليه فلا تكون ديناً عليه يطالب به ويحبس عليه إلا بإحدى هذين الشيئين فحينئذ تصير ديناً عليه فتأخذه منه جبراً، سواء كان غائباً أو حاضراً، لسواء أكلت من مال نفسها أو استدانت وأطلق المصنف فشمل المدة القليلة لكن ذكر في الغاية أن نفقة ما دون الشهر لا تسقط وعزاه إلى الذخيرة فكأنه جعل القليل مما لا يمكن التحرز عنه إذ لو سقطت بمضي اليسير من المدة لما تمكنت الأخذ من أصلاً اهـ. والمراد بالرضا اصطلاحهما على قدر معين للنفقة إما أصنافاً أو دراهم ولذا عبر الحدادي بالفرض والتقدير ; فإذا فرض لها الزوج شيئاً معيناً كل يوم ثم مضت مدة فإنها لا تسقط، فهذا هو المراد بقولهم ( أو الرضا»، وأما ما توهمه بعض حنفية العصر من أن المراد بالرضا أنه إذا مضت مدة بغير فرض ولا رضا ثم رضي الزوج بشيء فإنه يلزمه فخطأ ظاهر.
His statement: (And past maintenance is not obligatory except by judicial order or consent) because maintenance is a gift (silah) and not a consideration ('iwad) according to us. Thus its obligation is not firmly established except by judicial order, like a gift does not necessitate ownership except by a reinforcement, which is possession. And settlement (sulh) is like a judicial order because his authority over himself is stronger than the authority of the judge. Contrary to the dower (mahr) because it is a consideration for the marital bond. The meaning of 'its non-obligation' is that it is not a debt upon him; thus it does not become a debt upon him that can be demanded and imprisoned for except by one of these two things. Then it becomes a debt upon him, so she takes it from him forcibly, whether he is absent or present, whether she ate from her own wealth or borrowed. And the author's absolute expression includes a short period, but it is mentioned in al-Ghayah that maintenance for less than a month does not lapse, attributed to al-Dhakhirah. As if he considered the small amount as something not easily avoidable, because if it lapsed with the passage of a little time, she could never take it at all. The meaning of 'consent' is their mutual agreement on a specific amount of maintenance, either in kind or in dirhams. Hence al-Hadadi expressed it as 'fixing and estimating'. So if the husband fixed a specific amount each day and then time passed, it does not lapse. This is the intended meaning of their statement 'or consent'. As for what some contemporary Hanafis mistakenly understand – that consent means if some time passes without fixing or consent, and then the husband consents to something, it becomes obligatory – that is a clear error.
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage is a 'ruling with proof' (expansion probe) explaining a key principle of Hanafi family law: past maintenance (nafaqah) does not automatically accumulate as a debt on the husband. The author provides two proofs: (1) Maintenance is a 'silah' (gift) not an 'iwad' (exchange/consideration), so like a gift, it requires an additional act (qabd for gift, qada' for maintenance) to become binding. (2) This differs from mahr, which is a consideration for marriage and thus becomes a debt immediately. Therefore, maintenance only becomes a debt enforceable by the court if a judge has fixed it (qada') or if the husband and wife have mutually agreed on a specific amount (rida). The 'rida' here means a prior agreement on a fixed amount, not a retroactive approval. The author also notes that for very short periods (less than a month), some sources say it does not lapse even without qada' or rida, to avoid hardship. A common misunderstanding is that if time passes and then the husband later consents to pay something, that becomes obligatory; but the text clarifies that 'rida' must be a pre-agreed fixed amount, not post-hoc consent.

Key Terms
صلة (silah): A gift or voluntary payment, not an exchange (mu'awadah). Maintenance is classified as silah, not 'iwad.
عوض (iwad): Compensation or consideration in a contract, such as mahr for marital bond.
القضاء (al-qada'): A judicial order by a judge fixing the amount of maintenance.
الرضا (al-rida): Mutual agreement between husband and wife on a specific amount of maintenance (either in kind or money).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does past maintenance not become a debt without qada' or rida according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because maintenance is like mahr
B) Because maintenance is a gift (silah), not a consideration (iwad)
C) Because the husband must always agree first
D) Because maintenance is not obligatory at all

Key Takeaway
Past maintenance does not automatically become a debt in Hanafi law; it requires a judicial order or a prior agreed amount to be enforceable.

Judge's Modification of Maintenance and Validity of Settlement
Explains judge's power to adjust maintenance and validity of settlement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a judge may modify a maintenance decree and identify when a settlement between spouses on maintenance is valid according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
A maintenance decree can be revised for price changes or error; a settlement exceeding rights is only valid within the de minimis range of taghabun.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the Hanafi position on the flexibility of maintenance decrees and the limits of spousal settlements. The author explains that a judge's initial ruling is not final—it can be adjusted when prices fluctuate or if the initial estimate proves insufficient or excessive. Moreover, if a wife settles with her husband for more than her legal maintenance, the excess is only enforceable if it falls within the range that people normally overlook (taghabun). If the excess is beyond that, it is void, and the husband must pay standard maintenance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main rulings
The passage presents two distinct rulings: (1) the judge may modify a maintenance decree due to price changes or error, and (2) a settlement between spouses for more than the wife's legal maintenance is valid only within the taghabun limit.
These rulings are independent but related through the concept of fairness and the finality of judicial decrees.
2
Extract conditions for judge's modification
From the text, the judge's modification is triggered by: (a) a change in food prices (gala al-ta'am or rakhasa), or (b) an error in the initial estimate that results in insufficiency or excess. The judge must rectify the error to ensure adequacy for the wife or prevent undue burden on the husband.
The modification does not void the original decree entirely; the original estimate remains valid as a basis, but the amount is adjusted.
3
Extract condition for settlement validity
A settlement (sulh) between spouses on maintenance is valid if the excess over the wife's legal rights is within the range that people normally overlook (yataghābanu al-nās). If the excess is beyond that range, the increase is rejected (mardud).
The term 'taghabun' is a legal standard assessed by custom (urf).
4
Note the legal consequence
When the excess is beyond taghabun, the judge's decree is not voided; only the increase is voided. The husband must pay the maintenance of a woman like the wife (nafaqat al-mithl), and the original decree remains intact for the proper amount.
This preserves the stability of judicial decisions while allowing correction for unfairness.
5
Apply the principle consistently
If prices drop after a decree, the increase (the difference between the high-price amount and the current lower amount) is dropped, but the original decree itself is not voided. This ensures that maintenance does not fall off with the passage of time.
The author reasons: if the original decree were voided, the wife's maintenance would lapse, which is not intended.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن قلنا أنه المراد كما وقع التصريح به في الهداية فهو محمول على يسارها أيضاً، ومتى أمكن الحمل فلا تناقض وأشار المصنف إلى أن القاضي إذا فرض النفقة للمرأة فغلا الطعام أو رخص فإن القاضي يغير ذلك الحكم؛ كذا في الظهيرية وفي الذخيرة : وإذا فرض القاضي لها مالاً يكفيها فلها أن ترجع عن ذلك لأنه ظهر خطأ القاضي حيث قضى بما لا يكفيها فعليه أن يتدارك الخطأ بالقضاء لها بما يكفيها، وكذلك إذا فرض على الزوج زيادة على ما يكفيها فله أن يمتنع عن الزيادة .اهـ. وفي الخلاصة : لو صالحته على أكثر من حقوقها في النفقة والكسوة إن كان قدر ما يتغابن الناس في مثله ،جاز، وإن كان قدر ما لا يتغابن الناس فالزيادة مردودة ويلزمه نفقة مثلها ولا يبطل القضاء، فلو أن القاضي فرض لها النفقة والسعر غالي رخص ثم تسقط الزيادة، وهذا يدل على أنه لا يبطل القضاء وتبطل الزيادة اهـ. يعني لا يبطل أصل التقدير بزيادة السعر أو نقصانه حتى لو مضت مدة لا تسقط النفقة إذ لو بطل أصله لسقطت بمضي الزمان وسيأتي في مسائل الصلح عن النفقة قريباً إن شاء الله تعالى.
Even if we say that is the intended meaning as explicitly stated in al-Hidayah, it is interpreted with reference to her wealth as well. Whenever interpretation is possible, there is no contradiction. The author indicated that if the judge fixes maintenance for the woman and then food becomes expensive or cheap, the judge changes that ruling. Thus in al-Zahiriyyah and in al-Dhakhirah: If the judge fixed for her an amount sufficient for her, she may revoke that because the judge's error became apparent when he ruled with what is insufficient for her. So he must rectify the error by ruling for her what suffices her. Similarly, if he fixed for the husband an increase beyond what suffices her, the husband may refuse the increase. End quote. In al-Khulasa: If she settles with him for more than her rights in maintenance and clothing, if it is an amount regarding which people overlook similar amounts (taghabun), it is permissible. If it is an amount regarding which people do not overlook, the increase is rejected and he is liable for maintenance like her (maintenance of a woman like her), and the judge's decree is not voided. So if the judge fixed maintenance for her while the price was high, then it became cheap, the increase falls off. This indicates that the decree is not voided, and the increase is voided. End quote. That is, the original estimate is not voided by increase or decrease in price, so even if a period passes, the maintenance does not fall off, because if the original were voided, it would fall off with the passage of time. And soon it will come in the sections of settlement regarding maintenance, if Allah wills.
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage discusses the judge's authority to modify a maintenance decree when circumstances change, and the validity of settlements between spouses. The author explains that if prices fluctuate, the judge can adjust the amount. Similarly, if the judge's initial estimate was flawed, either party can seek correction. The key principle from al-Khulasa is that a settlement exceeding the legal maintenance is only valid if the excess is within the range that people normally overlook (taghabun). If the excess is beyond that, it is rejected, and the husband must pay the standard maintenance for a woman of her status. Additionally, when prices drop after a decree, the increase is dropped, but the original decree remains intact. This ensures stability while allowing adjustments for fairness.

Key Terms
يتغابن الناس (yataghābanu al-nās): The amount regarding which people normally overlook in transactions, considered a de minimis threshold for permissible excess in settlements.
صلح (ṣulḥ): A settlement or compromise between spouses on maintenance, which can be valid if within taghabun limits.

Key Takeaway
A judge may adjust maintenance for changing circumstances; a settlement exceeding legal rights is only valid within the de minimis taghabun limit, and the original decree remains intact.

Wife's Recourse for Fixed Maintenance After Borrowing Instruction
Intra-Hanafi dispute on wife's recourse after borrowing instruction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply al-Ramli's explanation to determine whether a wife can reclaim fixed maintenance when the husband instructs her to borrow.

Core Idea
A husband's instruction to borrow without explicit recourse turns her spending into a donation, waiving the fixed maintenance.

The general Hanafi rule is that after a judge fixes maintenance, the wife can reclaim it even if she borrows. However, a problematic case from al-Khaniyyah complicates this: when the husband specifically tells her to borrow and spend, she loses recourse unless he adds 'with recourse to me'. In this lesson, we examine al-Ramli's elegant resolution of this apparent conflict through the concept of donation (tabarru').

Guided Path
1
Understand the general rule
State the general Hanafi position: after a judge's decree, the wife can reclaim the fixed maintenance whether or not she stipulated recourse.
This is the Zahir al-Riwayah position.
2
Identify the problematic case
Read the case from al-Khaniyyah: husband says 'borrow each month such-and-such and spend on yourself'. The wife borrows and spends, but she has no recourse unless the husband says 'and you will have recourse to me for that'.
This seems to contradict the general rule.
3
Trace al-Ramli's reasoning
Al-Ramli explains that agency for borrowing is invalid, so the wife borrows on her own liability. Her compliance with the husband's order is interpreted as a donation (tabarru') because donation is the lesser of two possibilities (the other being that she expects reimbursement). Thus, she is spending from her own wealth as a gift, effectively waiving the fixed maintenance during that period.
The key is the implication of donation.
4
Identify the exception
If the husband adds 'with recourse to me', this negates the donation interpretation, and she can reclaim. Also, if the husband did not instruct borrowing at all, the general rule applies and she reclaims.
The presence of recourse stipulation preserves the debt nature.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فهذا هو المراد بقولهم أو الرضا) أيده في النهر بما يأتي عن الذخيرة اختلفا فيما مضى من وقت القضاء أو من وقت الصلح فالقول للزوج والبينة لها قال: ومقتضى ما في البحر لا يفهمه من له أدنى تأمل. وأما ما سيأتي من مسائل الصلح بلا قضاء ولا رضا فالمراد أنهما اصطلحا على شيء ثم مضت مدة بعده كما لا يخفى وظاهر المتون والشروح أن المرأة ترجع بالنفقة المفروضة، سواء شرط الرجوع لها أو لا، ويشكل عليه ما في الخانية والظهيرية القاضي إذا فرض للمرأة النفقة فقال الزوج استقرضي كل شهر كذا وأنفقي على نفسك ففعلت ليس لها أن ترجع على الزوج إلا أن يقول وترجعين بذلك على اهـ. ولم أر جواباً عنها ولعل المراد أنها لا ترجع بما استقرضت وإنما ترجع بما فرض لها لأن المأمور باستقراضه قد يكون أزيد أو . من خلاف الجنس وإن لم يؤول بذلك فهو غلط محض كما لا يخفى. وفي الظهيرية : إذا قال الرجل لآخر استدن علي لامرأتي وأنفق عليها كل شهر عشرة دراهم وقال أنفقت وقالت المرأة صدق لم يصدق على ذلك إلا أن يكون القاضي فرض لها النفقة فحينئذ يصدق لأنها أخذت بإذن القاضي، وكذا هذا في الأولاد الصغار اهـ. وأشار المصنف إلى أن عن النفقة قبل القضاء والصلح باطل لما في الواقعات وغيرها : المرأة إذا أبرأت الزوج النفقة بأن قالت أنت بريء من نفقتي أبداً ما كنت امرأتك فإن لم يفرض القاضي لها النفقة فالبراءة باطلة لأنها أبرأته قبل الوجوب، وإن كان فرض لها القاضي النفقة كل شهر عشرة دراهم صح الإبراء عن نفقة الشهر الأول ولم يصح عن نفقة ما مضي المسألة صحيح سوی ذلك من وجهه صلح عما لم يجب في أن الصلح بناء على ما ادعاه من خطأ ذلك الفهم غير وكان أنه الذمة. واعلم أنه يبنى على كونها لا تثبت ديناً في الذمة إلا بما ذكر أن الإبراء عنها قبل ذلك غير لما أنه إبراء قبل الوجوب قوله : (ثم مضت مدة بعده أي وليس المراد أن الصلح وقع بعد المدة قوله : ( ولعل المراد أنها لا ترجع بما استقرضت الخ) قال المقدسي أقول: الأحسن أن يوجه بأن التوكيل في القرض غير صحيح فاستقرضت على نفسها فلزمها، وإن قال على أن ترجعي علي كان هذا منه كاصطلاح على هذا المقدار فترجع عليه به ا.هـ. قلت وفيه غفلة عن كون موضوع بعد فرض القاضي وقد مر أنها ترجع بعده، سواء أكلت من مال نفسها أو استدانت، فإذا لم الاستقراض ما الداعي إلى عدم الرجوع بالمفروض ؟ فالإشكال بحاله. وأجاب الرملي عن الإشكال بأن الزوج لما قال لها استقرضي وأنفقي على نفسك كانت مستقرضة على نفسها لعدم صحة التوكيل بالاستقراض وقصدها امتثال كلامه وكلامه موجب للزوم الدين عليها لا عليه وأمرها بأن تنفق ما استدانته على نفسها لا عليه فيحتمل التبرع وغيره، والتبرع أدنى الحالتين فيحمل عليه فكأنه أمرها بالإنفاق على نفسها من مالها متبرعة فامتثلت أمره فكان إسقاطاً للفرض في مدة الاستدانة والنفقة مما استدانته بخلاف ما إذا لم يقل لها ذلك لعدم العلة المذكورة فبقي فرض القاضي وهو موجب للرجوع عليه. والحاصل أن قوله استقرضي وأنفقي وإجابتها له إضراب عن الفرض منها . وانظر إلى قوله إلا أن يقول وترجعين بذلك علي» لأنه ينفي التبرع المستفاد من ذلك وإذا لم يوجد يصح ذلك بقي الفرض لعدم ما يستفاد منه التبرع فتأمله ا هـ .
His statement: (This is the intended meaning of their statement 'or mutual consent') was supported in al-Nahr by what comes from al-Dhakhirah: They disagreed regarding what has passed from the time of the judge's decree or from the time of settlement; the husband's word is taken and she has the evidence. He said: And the implication of what is in al-Bahr is not understood by anyone with the least reflection. As for what will come later regarding cases of settlement without decree or consent, the meaning is that they agreed upon something and then a period passed thereafter, as is not hidden. And the apparent meaning of the texts and commentaries is that the woman reclaims the fixed maintenance, whether the right of recourse was stipulated or not. But what is in al-Khaniyyah and al-Zahiriyyah is problematic: If the judge fixed maintenance for the woman, and the husband said, 'Borrow each month such-and-such and spend on yourself,' and she did so, she has no recourse against the husband unless he says, 'And you will have recourse to me for that.' End quote. I have not seen an answer to it. Perhaps the intended meaning is that she does not reclaim what she borrowed but rather reclaims what was fixed for her, because what she was ordered to borrow may be more or of a different type. But if it does not reduce to that, it is pure error, as is not hidden. In al-Zahiriyyah: If a man says to another, 'Take a loan upon me for my wife and spend on her every month ten dirhams,' and he says 'I spent,' and the woman says 'he spoke the truth,' he is not believed unless the judge had fixed maintenance for her; then he is believed because she took with the judge's permission. Similarly for minor children. End quote. The author indicated that release from maintenance before decree and settlement is invalid, as in al-Waqi'at etc.: If a woman releases the husband from maintenance by saying, 'You are free from my maintenance forever as long as I am your wife,' then if the judge did not fix maintenance for her, the release is invalid because she released him before obligation. If the judge fixed maintenance for her at ten dirhams per month, the release is valid for the first month's maintenance but not for what has passed [؟] the case is valid otherwise from its face [؟] settlement for what is not yet due [؟]... And know that it is based on the fact that it is not established as a debt in the liability except by what was mentioned, so release before that is not valid because it is release before obligation. His statement: (then a period passed thereafter) meaning it is not that the settlement occurred after the period. His statement: (and perhaps the intended meaning is that she does not reclaim what she borrowed etc.) Al-Maqdisi said: I say the best approach is to explain that the agency for borrowing is not valid, so she borrowed for herself and it became binding on her. If he said 'with recourse to me', this from him is like an agreement on that amount, so she can reclaim it from him. End quote. I say: There is in it neglect of the fact that the subject is after the judge's decree, and it has been mentioned that she reclaims after it, whether she ate from her own wealth or borrowed. So if borrowing is not valid, what is the reason for non-recourse for the fixed amount? The problem remains. Al-Ramli answered the problem by saying that when the husband said 'borrow and spend on yourself', she was borrowing for herself due to the invalidity of agency for borrowing, and she intended to comply with his words, and his words necessitate the binding of the debt on her, not on him. And his order that she spend what she borrowed on herself, not on him, so it is possible that it is donation (tabarru') or otherwise, and donation is the lesser of the two cases, so it is interpreted as such. So it is as if he ordered her to spend on herself from her wealth as a donation, and she complied with his order, so it was a dropping of the fixed maintenance during the period of borrowing, and the maintenance is from what she borrowed. Unlike the case where he did not say that to her, because there is no reason mentioned, so the judge's fixed maintenance remains and it necessitates recourse. The summary is that his saying 'borrow and spend' and her compliance is a departure from the fixed maintenance. And look at his statement 'unless he says: and you will have recourse to me for that', because it negates the donation derived from that. And if that does not occur, the fixed maintenance remains because there is nothing from which donation is derived. So reflect. End quote.
Source pages p. 317

Commentary
This passage addresses two issues: the wife's right to reclaim the fixed maintenance after a judge's decree, and the validity of release (ibra') from maintenance. The general ruling from the texts is that the woman can reclaim the fixed maintenance, whether she stipulated recourse or not. However, a problematic case from al-Khaniyyah states that if the husband tells her to borrow and spend, she cannot reclaim unless he explicitly says 'with recourse to me'. The author initially struggles to answer, but later presents al-Ramli's explanation: when the husband tells her to borrow, she borrows on her own behalf because agency for borrowing is invalid. Her compliance is interpreted as a donation (tabarru'), thus waiving the fixed maintenance. If he adds 'with recourse to me', it negates donation and she can reclaim. The second issue is release: release before judge's decree or settlement is invalid because the maintenance is not yet a debt. After a decree, release is valid for the first month (already accrued) but not for future months, as they are not yet owed.

Key Terms
إبراء (ibrā’): Release or discharge from an obligation; here, a wife releasing the husband from maintenance.
استقراض (istiqrāḍ): Borrowing money; in this context, the husband telling the wife to borrow for her own expenses.
تبرع (tabarru‘): Voluntary donation or gratuitous act; here, the wife's spending from borrowed money is interpreted as donation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Ramli, why does the wife lose recourse to the fixed maintenance when the husband tells her to borrow and spend without adding 'with recourse'?
A) Because she did not actually spend the money on herself.
B) Because agency for borrowing is invalid, so she borrows on her own liability, and her compliance is interpreted as a donation.
C) Because the judge's decree becomes void when the husband speaks.
D) Because she cannot prove she borrowed the exact amount.

Key Takeaway
A husband's instruction to borrow without explicit 'with recourse' converts the wife's spending into a donation, barring her from reclaiming the fixed maintenance.

Nafaqah — Maintenance
beginner
5 min
Validity of Release (Ibra') from Fixed Maintenance
Hanafi ruling on release from maintenance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between valid and invalid releases from maintenance according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Release from maintenance is invalid before a debt exists; after a judge's decree, only accrued maintenance can be released.

The passage also addresses a second issue: the validity of a wife's release (ibra') from her right to maintenance. The Hanafi ruling hinges on whether the maintenance has become a debt in the husband's liability. Before a judge's decree or settlement, the maintenance is not yet a debt, so release is null. After a decree, the maintenance becomes a debt as it accrues; thus, release is only valid for the already accrued month but not for future months.

Guided Path
1
Understand the principle of debt for release
Release (ibra') requires an existing debt. If the maintenance has not been fixed by a judge or settlement, it is not a debt, so release is invalid.
This is based on the rule that ibra' before obligation is invalid.
2
Identify the two scenarios
Scenario 1: No judge's decree – release is completely invalid. Scenario 2: After decree – maintenance becomes a cumulative debt.
The decree crystallizes past maintenance into a debt.
3
Apply the rule to accrued vs future maintenance
For the first month after decree, the maintenance is already owed (debt), so release is valid. For future months, the maintenance is not yet owed, so release is invalid.
This is analogous to releasing a debt that does not yet exist.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

When is a wife's release from maintenance considered valid according to this passage?

Nafaqah — Maintenance
intermediate
8 min
Wife's Recourse for Borrowed Maintenance: The Tabarru' Nuance
Resolving a conflict between general ruling and a problematic case from al-Khaniyya

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on a wife's recourse for maintenance when she borrows on her husband's instruction, and apply al-Ramli's istihsan-based resolution to distinguish between donation and debt.

Core Idea
A husband's instruction to borrow implies donation unless he says 'and you will recover'; no debt arises for that loan.

In Hanafi law, a judge-fixed maintenance becomes a debt on the husband, recoverable by the wife regardless of how she covers her expenses. However, a problematic case from al-Khaniyya introduces a nuance: if the husband specifically tells his wife to borrow and spend, does she still have recourse? This lesson unpacks the apparent conflict and the sophisticated resolution offered by later Hanafi jurists, particularly al-Ramli, using the principle of istihsan (juristic preference) and the presumption of tabarru' (donation).

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
Recognize that the fixed maintenance (nafaqa mafruda) is a debt on the husband; the wife can recover it whether she used her own money or borrowed.
This is the apparent ruling of the matn and commentaries.
2
Identify the problematic case
From al-Khaniyya and al-Zahiriya: if the husband says 'istaqridi wa anfiqi' (borrow and spend) without adding 'and you will recover', she has no recourse. Why does this contradict the general rule?
The conflict triggers the need for a resolution.
3
Examine al-Maqdisi's attempted resolution
Al-Maqdisi argued that agency for borrowing is invalid, so the wife borrows on her own credit; the husband's instruction is like a settlement (sulh) on that amount.
The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq critiques this because it ignores the judge's order.
4
Analyze al-Ramli's final resolution
Al-Ramli uses istihsan: the husband's words imply donation (tabarru') because the wife acts on her own, not as agent. The weaker probability (tabarru') is adopted, suspending the debt during the borrowing period.
The judge's order remains for other periods; only the specific loan is considered donation.
5
Identify the exception clause
If the husband says 'and you will recover', the implication of tabarru' is negated, and the original fixed maintenance debt applies to that borrowing too.
This phrase restores recourse.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما ما سيأتي من مسائل الصلح بلا قضاء ولا رضا فالمراد أنهما اصطلحا على شيء ثم مضت مدة بعده كما لا يخفى وظاهر المتون والشروح أن المرأة ترجع بالنفقة المفروضة، سواء شرط الرجوع لها أو لا، ويشكل عليه ما في الخانية والظهيرية القاضي إذا فرض للمرأة النفقة فقال الزوج استقرضي كل شهر كذا وأنفقي على نفسك ففعلت ليس لها أن ترجع على الزوج إلا أن يقول وترجعين بذلك علي اهـ. ولم أر جواباً عنها ولعل المراد أنها لا ترجع بما استقرضت وإنما ترجع بما فرض لها لأن المأمور باستقراضه قد يكون أزيد أو من خلاف الجنس وإن لم يؤول بذلك فهو غلط محض كما لا يخفى. وفي الظهيرية : إذا قال الرجل لآخر استدن علي لامرأتي وأنفق عليها كل شهر عشرة دراهم وقال أنفقت وقالت المرأة صدق لم يصدق على ذلك إلا أن يكون القاضي فرض لها النفقة فحينئذ يصدق لأنها أخذت بإذن القاضي، وكذا هذا في الأولاد الصغار اهـ. وأشار المصنف إلى أن عن النفقة قبل القضاء والصلح باطل لما في الواقعات وغيرها : المرأة إذا أبرأت الزوج النفقة بأن قالت أنت بريء من نفقتي أبداً ما كنت امرأتك فإن لم يفرض القاضي لها النفقة فالبراءة باطلة لأنها أبرأته قبل الوجوب، وإن كان فرض لها القاضي النفقة كل شهر عشرة دراهم صح الإبراء عن نفقة الشهر الأول ولم يصح عن نفقة ما سوى ذلك من وجهه [؟] صحيح [؟] أن الصلح بناء على ما ادعاه من خطأ ذلك الفهم غير [؟] [؟] أنه الذمة. واعلم أنه يبنى على كونها لا تثبت ديناً في الذمة إلا بما ذكر أن الإبراء عنها قبل ذلك غير لما أنه إبراء قبل الوجوب قوله : (ثم مضت مدة بعده أي وليس المراد أن الصلح وقع بعد المدة قوله : ( ولعل المراد أنها لا ترجع بما استقرضت الخ) قال المقدسي أقول: الأحسن أن يوجه بأن التوكيل في القرض غير صحيح فاستقرضت على نفسها فلزمها، وإن قال على أن ترجعي علي كان هذا منه كاصطلاح على هذا المقدار فترجع عليه به ا.هـ. قلت وفيه غفلة عن كون موضوع بعد فرض القاضي وقد مر أنها ترجع بعده، سواء أكلت من مال نفسها أو استدانت، فإذا لم الاستقراض ما الداعي إلى عدم الرجوع بالمفروض ؟ فالإشكال بحاله. وأجاب الرملي عن الإشكال بأن الزوج لما قال لها استقرضي وأنفقي على نفسك كانت مستقرضة على نفسها لعدم صحة التوكيل بالاستقراض وقصدها امتثال كلامه وكلامه موجب للزوم الدين عليها لا عليه وأمرها بأن تنفق ما استدانته على نفسها لا عليه فيحتمل التبرع وغيره، والتبرع أدنى الحالتين فيحمل عليه فكأنه أمرها بالإنفاق على نفسها من مالها متبرعة فامتثلت أمره فكان إسقاطاً للفرض في مدة الاستدانة والنفقة مما استدانته بخلاف ما إذا لم يقل لها ذلك لعدم العلة المذكورة فبقي فرض القاضي وهو موجب للرجوع عليه. والحاصل أن قوله استقرضي وأنفقي وإجابتها له إضراب عن الفرض منها . وانظر إلى قوله إلا أن يقول وترجعين بذلك علي» لأنه ينفي التبرع المستفاد من ذلك وإذا لم يوجد ذلك بقي الفرض لعدم ما يستفاد منه التبرع فتأمله ا هـ .
As for what is coming regarding cases of settlement without a court order or consent, the meaning is that they agreed on something and then a period passed after it, as is not hidden. The apparent meaning of the matn and commentaries is that the woman returns (recovers) the fixed maintenance, whether or not the right of recourse is stipulated for her. But a problem arises regarding what is in al-Khaniyya and al-Zahiriya: when the judge fixed maintenance for the woman and the husband said, 'Borrow each month such-and-such and spend on yourself,' and she did so, she has no right to recourse against the husband unless he says, 'And you will recover thereby' etc. I have not seen an answer for this. Perhaps the meaning is that she does not recover what she borrowed, but she recovers what was fixed for her, because what she was ordered to borrow may be more or of a different kind. If it does not lead to that, it is pure error, as is not hidden. In al-Zahiriya: If a man said to another, 'Borrow for me for my wife and spend on her every month ten dirhams,' and he said 'I spent,' and the woman said 'true,' he is not believed regarding that unless the judge had fixed maintenance for her, then he is believed because she took with the judge's permission. Similarly for minor children etc. The author indicated that maintenance before a court order and settlement is invalid because...
Source pages p. 317

Commentary
This passage deals with a crucial nuance in the Hanafi law of maintenance (nafaqa). The general principle is that when a judge fixes maintenance, it becomes a debt (dayn) on the husband, and the wife can recover it from him, whether she spent her own money or borrowed. However, a problematic case arises from al-Khaniyya and al-Zahiriya: if the judge fixed maintenance, but the husband tells the wife to borrow and spend (without specifying recourse), she cannot recover from husband unless he explicitly says 'and you will recover thereby.' The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq notes this problem. Al-Maqdisi tries to resolve it by saying that agency (tawkil) for borrowing is invalid, so the wife borrows on her own credit, and the husband's instruction to her is a kind of agreement (sulh) on that amount. But the author criticizes this because the judge's order already made it recoverable. Al-Ramli gives a more thorough answer: the husband's words 'borrow and spend' imply that she is to spend as a donation (tabarru'), because she is acting on her own and not as his agent; thus the judge's order is temporarily suspended during the borrowing period. If the husband adds 'and you will recover,' then the tabarru' is negated, and the original order stands. The bottom line: the husband's instruction to borrow without express recourse negates the duty to pay back that specific loan, but the general maintenance debt remains for other periods. This is a delicate distinction based on istihsan.

Key Terms
النفقة المفروضة (al-nafaqa al-mafruda): Maintenance fixed by a judge, which becomes a debt on the husband.
استقرض (istaqrada): To borrow money; here the wife borrows on her own account.
تبرع (tabarru'): Donation; here implies the wife's spending without claim for repayment.
إستحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; a method of resolving a legal issue by considering equity and the underlying purpose of the law, sometimes departing from a literal analogy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Ramli's resolution, why does the wife not have recourse for the borrowed amount when the husband said 'istaqridi wa anfiqi'?
A) Because agency for borrowing is invalid, so the wife is a donor.
B) Because the judge's order is suspended during the borrowing period.
C) Because the husband's words imply donation (tabarru'), and donation is the default interpretation.
D) Because borrowed money is not considered maintenance.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a husband's instruction to his wife to borrow and spend on herself without explicit 'recourse' wording turns that borrowing into a donation, negating her right to recover that specific amount, though the underlying maintenance obligation remains.

Renunciation of Future Maintenance in Hanafi Fiqh
Ruling on renunciation of future maintenance and the analogy with slave hire

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Hanafi law restricts renunciation of future maintenance to one month and apply the qiyas analogy to the slave hire case.

Core Idea
Future maintenance is not a debt until each month begins; thus, renouncing it in advance only covers the first upcoming month.

In Hanafi fiqh, the institution of ibra' (renunciation) operates only on existing debts. Maintenance (nafaqah) for a wife is a recurring obligation that arises month by month. The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies that if a wife attempts to renounce all future maintenance in one statement, the renunciation is effective only for the first month. This ruling is derived through qiyas (analogical reasoning) with the case of a slave hired out by monthly wages.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the source text to find the specific ruling: what happens when a wife says she releases her husband from future maintenance for a year or forever.
The ruling states only one month's maintenance is waived.
2
Understand the legal cause (illa)
The judge fixes maintenance per month based on a meaning that renews monthly. Each month's obligation is separate and arises only at the start of that month.
Both the obligation and its cause (the month) renew each month.
3
Follow the qiyas analogy
The text analogizes to a slave hired for monthly wages: if the employer releases the slave from all future hire forever, only one month's hire is waived.
The common illa is that the obligation for each month is independent and not yet in existence for future months.
4
Apply to the wife's case
Similarly, a wife's renunciation of future maintenance for a year only covers the first month because subsequent months' obligations have not yet accrued.
If she releases both past and future, past maintenance is fully waived, but future only for one month.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشهور. وكذا لو قالت أبرأتك عن نفقة سنة لم يبدأ إلا من نفقة شهر واحد لأن القاضي لما فرض نفقة كل شهر فإنما فرض لمعنى يتجدد بتجدد الشهر فما لم يتجدد الشهر لا يتجدد الفرض، وما لم يتجدد الفرض لا تصير نفقة الشهر الثاني واجباً ولو قالت بعدما مكثت أشهراً أبرأتك من نفقة ما مضى وما يستقبل يبرأ من نفقة ما مضى ويبرأ من نفقة ما يستقبل بقدر نفقة شهر ولا يبرأ زيادة على ذلك، وهو نظير من أجر عبده من رجل كل شهر بعشرة دراهم ثم أبرأه من أجرة الغلام أبداً لا يبرأ إلا من أجرة شهر اهـ .
The months. Likewise if she said, 'I have released you from the maintenance of a year,' nothing begins except from the maintenance of one month, because when the judge fixed the maintenance of each month, he fixed it for a meaning that renews with the renewal of the month. So as long as the month has not renewed, the obligation does not renew, and as long as the obligation has not renewed, the maintenance of the second month does not become obligatory. And if she said after several months had passed, 'I have released you from the maintenance of what has passed and what will come,' he is released from the maintenance of what has passed and from the maintenance of what will come to the extent of one month's maintenance, and no more. This is analogous to someone who hired out his slave to a man for ten dirhams each month, then released him from the hire of the slave forever; he is only released from one month's hire.
Source pages p. 318

Commentary
This passage clarifies the Hanafi ruling on renunciation (ibra') of maintenance. The key point is that maintenance for each month is a separate obligation that arises only when the month begins. Therefore, if a wife attempts to renounce all future maintenance in advance (e.g., for a full year), the renunciation is only effective for the first month. This is because the judge's order fixes maintenance with a recurring cause (sabab) that regenerates each month; the obligation for the second month does not exist yet at the time of renunciation. The analogy of hiring a slave with monthly wages is used to illustrate: a general renunciation of all future hire only covers the first month's payment due immediately. This ruling is consistent with the principle that ibra' (like a gift) cannot be applied to a debt that does not yet exist. The text also notes that if the wife says after several months have passed, 'I release you from past and future,' then past obligations are covered (since they existed) and future obligations only up to one month (the next one to become due).

Key Terms
إبراء (ibra'): Renunciation or release of a debt; a unilateral discharge.
فرض (fard): In this context, the judge's fixing of maintenance as an obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A wife says to her husband, 'I release you from the maintenance of this year and all future years.' According to the passage, how many months' maintenance is waived?
A) All months for this year and future years
B) Only the first month after the statement
C) The entire current year only
D) None, because the renunciation is invalid

Key Takeaway
Renunciation (ibra') of future maintenance is effective only for the first upcoming month because each month's obligation arises only at its start.
