Nafaqah — Maintenance
intermediate
8 min
Compelling the Mother to Breastfeed: Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Commentary on ruling that mother is not compelled legally, with discussion of ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on compelling a mother to breastfeed, identify the conditions under which she is legally compelled (qada'an), and distinguish between the initial zahir al-riwayah view and the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
A mother is not legally forced to breastfeed unless the child refuses all others or the family lacks resources.

The matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq states that a mother is not compelled to breastfeed. However, this ruling has an internal Hanafi dispute: is it absolute or conditional? In this passage, the commentator expands on the ikhtilaf, weighing the initial position (no compulsion even if the child refuses) against the later relied-upon view that compulsion applies when necessary for the child's well-being.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position from the matn
Identify the base ruling: 'ولا تجبر أمه لترضع' — the mother is not compelled legally. Understand that the commentator explains she is still religiously obliged (diyanatan).
This is the starting point of the ikhtilaf.
2
Identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Note the two positions: (1) Zahir al-Riwayah: no compulsion even if the child refuses others (al-Zayla'i, al-Itqani). (2) Later view: compulsion when the child refuses all others or when the father has no wealth (al-Hidayah, al-Khaniyya, Fath al-Qadir).
The ikhtilaf is about the scope of ijbar.
3
Analyse the dalil for the initial position
The initial view argues that the child can be nourished by oil and other liquids, so there is no risk of harm (ḥaraj), hence no need for compulsion.
This is a qiyas jali analogy to nafaqah.
4
Examine the tarjih and its reasoning
The later tarjih (preference) is for compulsion in the specified cases. The reasoning is that restricting an infant to oil and drink causes illness and death (Fath al-Qadir). Also, if the father and child have no wealth, compulsion is by consensus (al-Khaniyya).
The later view prioritises the child's welfare.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: Under the earlier view, the mother could refuse even if the child only accepts her. Under the fatwa view, she must breastfeed in that scenario or if the family is penniless.
The mufta bihi has real-world impact on mothers and judges.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولا تجبر أمه لترضع لأنه كالنفقة وهي على الأب وعسى لا تقدر فلا تجبر عليه قضاء وتؤمر به ديانة لأنه من باب الاستخدام وهو واجب عليها ديانة كما قدمناه. أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان الأب لا يجد من يرضعه أو كان الولد لا يأخذ ثدي غيرها. ونقل الزيلعي والإتقاني أنه ظاهر الرواية لأنه يتغذى بالدهن وغيره من المائعات فلا يؤدي إلى ضياعه، ونقل عدم الإجبار في هذه الحالة في المجتبى عن البعض ثم قال والأصح أنها تجبر عند الكل اهـ . وجزم به في الهداية، وفي الخانية وعليه الفتوى، وذكر في فتح القدير أنه الأصوب لأن قصر الرضيع الذي لم يأنس الطعام على الدهن والشراب سبب تمريضه وموته اهـ. وفي الخانية : وإن لم يكن للأب ولا للولد الصغير مال تجبر الأم على الإرضاع عند الكل اهـ. فجعل يستحق النفقة، وانظر ما كتبناه هناك أيضاً يظهر لك الأمر
His statement: 'And his mother is not compelled to breastfeed' because it is like nafaqah and it is upon the father, and perhaps she is unable, so she is not compelled judicially and she is commanded religiously because it is from the category of service (istikhdam) and it is obligatory upon her religiously as we have previously mentioned. He made it absolute, so it includes when the father cannot find someone to breastfeed or the child does not take the breast of anyone else. Al-Zayla'i and al-Itqani reported that it is Zahir al-Riwayah because he is nourished by oil and other liquids so it does not lead to his loss. And it was reported that there is no compulsion in this case in al-Mujtaba from some, then he said the correct view is that she is compelled according to everyone. And it was firmly stated in al-Hidayah, and in al-Khaniyya and upon it is the fatwa. And it was mentioned in Fath al-Qadir that it is most correct because restricting the infant who has not become accustomed to food to oil and drink is a cause of his illness and death. And in al-Khaniyya: If the father and the minor child have no wealth, the mother is compelled to breastfeed according to everyone. Then he said: So she deserves nafaqah. And look at what we wrote there also, it will become clear to you.
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the matn ruling 'ولا تجبر أمه لترضع' from Kanz al-Daqaiq. The commentator explains the legal position: the mother is not compelled by a judge (qada'an) to breastfeed her child because she may be unable, but she is religiously obligated (diyanatan) to do so. The proof is that breastfeeding is analogous to nafaqah (maintenance), which is the father's duty; also, it is a form of service (istikhdam) that is morally required. However, the commentator notes an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: some early authorities (like those reported in al-Mujtaba) held that she is not compelled even when the child refuses others, but the relied-upon opinion (mufta bihi) is that she is compelled in such cases because restricting the child to oil and liquid leads to illness. This is confirmed in al-Hidayah, al-Khaniyya, and Fath al-Qadir. A further condition is that if the father and child have no wealth, the mother is compelled by consensus (ind al-kull) to breastfeed. The passage ends with a reference to the author's other writings.

Key Terms
الإجبار (al-ijbar): Legal compulsion by a judge (qada'an) to perform an act.
الرضاع (al-rida'): Breastfeeding of an infant by a woman.
النفقة (al-nafaqah): Maintenance covering food, clothing, and shelter legally required.
الاستخدام (al-istikhdam): Service (like breastfeeding) that is morally required but not legally compelled.
ديانة (diyanatan): Religious obligation not enforceable by a judge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school, when is the mother legally compelled to breastfeed?
A) Only when the father has money to pay her
B) When the child refuses all wet nurses except his mother
C) Never, because breastfeeding is only a moral obligation
D) When the mother demands payment

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi holds that a mother is legally compelled to breastfeed when the child refuses all others or when the family lacks wealth; otherwise the obligation is only religious.
